## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables correspond to a constitutive law mapping strain (epsilon) and temperature (T) to stress (sigma), typical of elasticity/plasticity and thermoelastic/viscoplastic material models where stiffness and flow stress soften or change with temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, temperature effectively constant)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature over a limited range)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (accounts for thermal expansion strain that reduces/increases mechanical strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinearity in stress–strain curve)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-like in 1D surrogate): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 / (1 + c2 * epsilon)) (captures increasing tangent stiffness with strain using a rational term)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type implicit surrogate (explicit approximation): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) (smooth transition from elastic to plastic-like behavior without an explicit yield point)
- Power-law strain hardening with thermal prefactor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * Abs(epsilon)**c3 (strength scales with strain via a power law and changes with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening of flow stress: sigma = c0 * Abs(epsilon)**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (often c2 < 0 to represent softening as temperature increases)
- Johnson–Cook-like (reduced, no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (work hardening multiplied by a thermal softening factor approximated by a polynomial)
- Saturating hardening (Voce-like): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * Abs(epsilon)))) * (c3 + c4 * exp(c5 * T)) (hardening saturates with strain; temperature modifies overall level)
- Eyring/thermally activated form (stress grows with inverse temperature): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * Abs(epsilon)) * exp(c2 / (T + c3)) (thermally activated resistance; strong T-sensitivity)
- Bilinear/piecewise elastic–plastic surrogate (smooth): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(1 + exp(c2 * (Abs(epsilon) - c3))) (approximates yield onset and post-yield hardening smoothly)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; adding T-dependence usually enters through an effective modulus factor multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal expansion effects → sigma depends on (epsilon minus a term proportional to T); this appears as an offset in strain inside parentheses.
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative factors that decrease with T (often exp(c*T) with negative c, or low-order polynomials in T) applied to the strain-dependent part.
- Work hardening behavior → sigma increases with Abs(epsilon) using power laws or saturating exponentials (e.g., 1 - exp(-c*Abs(epsilon))).
- Smooth yield transition without explicit piecewise definitions → log(1+exp(k*(Abs(epsilon)-eps0))) or rational forms that change slope around a characteristic strain.
- Need for symmetry in tension/compression (if sign not distinguished) → dependence on Abs(epsilon) rather than epsilon.
- Strong temperature sensitivity near low T (activated processes) → functions involving exp(c/(T+c0)) or similar inverse-temperature sensitivity.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity → products like f(epsilon)*g(T) are common because stiffness/flow stress scaling with T often modulates the entire stress–strain curve.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
```

```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) + c5*epsilon**c4*(T - K)
```

This gives:
```
-c0*c1*epsilon*T + c0*(c1*K + c3)*epsilon + c5*T*epsilon**c4 - c5*K*epsilon**c4
```

Let me define new constants:
- A = c5 = 5.2295 (coefficient of T*epsilon^c4)
- B = c4 = 0.9585 (power of epsilon)
- C = -c0*c1 = -23.788 * 0.05042 = -1.1994 (coefficient of epsilon*T)
- D = c0*(c1*K + c3) = 23.788*(0.05042*330.2 + 1) = 23.788*(17.645) = 419.76 (coefficient of epsilon)
- E = -c5*K = -5.2295*330.2 = -1726.8 (coefficient of epsilon^c4)

So GT = A*T*epsilon^B + C*T*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

GT = T*(A*epsilon^B + C*epsilon) + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

The basis functions in GT are:
1. T*epsilon^0.9585
2. T*epsilon (i.e., T*epsilon^1)
3. epsilon
4. epsilon^0.9585

Note that T*epsilon = T*epsilon^1, and since c4 ≈ 0.9585, epsilon^c4 ≠ epsilon^1. These are distinct basis functions.

- `T*c2` is a pure T term (no epsilon dependence) - this doesn't match any GT term unless c2=0.
- If c2=0, we lose the T*epsilon term unless it appears elsewhere.

Could any rational terms like `c/(c*epsilon + c)` produce a T*epsilon term? No, those don't involve T.
